Saturday, January 1, 1938

Got a lot of work done on the annual census today, between calls etc. Also football.
____________________________________________________________
(May 28th continued)

Hunted at 2 points near Paradise Camp, Mono Co. (foot of Sherwin grade) and got skellies, utas and a collard lizard in brush and rocks.

There were no DOR snakes around Bishop as thee were last summer. We reached Bishop in the early afternoon but found the auto camps already fulled because of the fishing crowd and decided to go on south which was probably wise as the season was evidently delayed and it was too cold to expect snakes out at night.

We drove back up the road toward Laws and beyond for a couple of mile and rested awhile. It seems to be possible sidewinder territory beyond the irrigated section and I see no real reason to doubt the MVZ record. The flat is fairly sandy and there is an occasional hummock. We pickled all specimens taken thus far from 5 until 6 and got everything in good shape. Turned back 11 mile mi. N of Bishop. It was now 6 p.m. and getting windy.
continued on Jan. 2)

Sunday, January 2, 1938

Phil left this morning at 8:15. Chapman Grant called this afternoon to discuss his new Jamaica ??? Also Bob Hoard his proposed MA study of rattlesnake breeding.

Spent the morning on the census and finished the 1937 tabulation both by months and by years.

Charles Shaw called up and said he caught a small ??? today, and many ???

________________________________________________
Continued from Jan. 1
There wer no Joshua Trees on the mountain sides that we could see hereabout so no reason to expect Xantusia vigilis so far north.

We passed Bishop southbound at 6:10, 69 degrees F.

1 Red Racer L. DOR 3 miles S of Bishop, grass

1 Red Racer L. DOR 4 miles so of Bishop, grass-brush

1 Red Racer L. DOR Keough HOt Springs, Inyo Co, brush

1 Red Racer L. DOR Keough Hot Springs, Inyo Co, brush

Big Pine at 6:35 72 degrees

1 Gopher M DOR Aberdeen, Inyo Co, grass-brush

1 Red Racer DOR Aberdeen, Inyo Co, brush
Independence at 7:15

Lone Pine at 7:45, 72 degrees, almost dark

1 Longnose L COR Cartago, Inyo Co, 71 degrees brush

Quite dark. 8:10

(Continued on January 3)

Tuesday, January 4, 1938

5 cards and 1 questionnaire received
______________________________________________________
(May 28th continued from Jan. 3rd)
Thought this one had been run over, but evidently not as he lived. 10:45, 60 degrees F

1 Red Racer L DOR Atolia low brush
San Berniadino Co. (These ecological notes were secured next day by going back in the same road).

1 Gopher L DOR 8 mi. N. of Kramer, S.B. Co greasewood brush.

1 Longnose DOR Kramer, brushy desert

1 Gopher L DOR Haws, S.B. Co.,
Brushy desert. Saved.

1 Arizona Small DOR Mace, S.B. Co., Brushy desert.

1 Platyrhinos DOR Mace, S.B. Co., Brushy desert
Reached Barstow at 12:30. Cold and windy 67°. All auto camps filled. Finally put up at the Beacon Inn and pickled specimens until after 1 AM. Pretty tired.
This night started out fairly well but proved ??? toward the end because of the rapidly falling temperature (considerably below that at Barstow in most parts). Traveled fast twoard the last as it so

(Continued on Jan. 5)

late and we were very tired.

Miles today 425. Miles after dark - evening desert drive 160

A fairly good day but the weather too cool and unsettled.

Thursday, January 6, 1938

7 cards returned today.
________________________________________________________
(May 29 continued)
1 CAlly ????, 2 whips collected 6 mi SW of Spangler, S.B. Co.

Looks good here for night collecting. Cally seen, also leopard 6 mi. NW of Spangler. Collected near here and got a chuck, utas, magistes, etc. This was fine rocky country.

Cally seen 6 miles SW of Westend, S.B. Co. Also ???? here. It is a sandy desert.

Saw chucks and callies in Porson Canyon SW of Westend. There are sand dunes near here which look good.

Went a little north of the big potash plant at Trona and then turned back. It was quite warm. All of this road looks good, and probably the road to Ballarat and Death Valley is ok. It is oiled at the start.

Cally seen at Trona.

Cally and Uta Collected 4 mi SW of Westend, S.B. Co.

1 Spotted nite DOR L 9 mi SW of Westend, Brushy desert - no rocks! Also cally collected here.

Uta collected 10 mi SW of Westend.
(Continued on Jan. 7)

Saturday, January 8, 1938

Spent the day on the annual audit for income tax, also cleaned up the Outdoor Life's purchased last February. Bad cold and feeling too rotten to do anything else.

Shaw worked today.

3 cards and a questionnaire received.
_____________________________________________________________
(May 29 continued from Jan 7)

1 Platyrhins DOR Penshaw S.B. Co.

Sunday, January 9, 1938

Feeling too lousy from a cold to do constructive work today. Finished the old Outdoor Lifes. Then spent the rest of the day and evening mapping Game Warden rattler records and made some progress. Sent out 7 cards for more data to:

J.L. Down, Douglas, Wyo

J.W. Drummond, Wray, Co

Joe Garner, Shoshone, Idaho

Frank Starina, Hardin, Mont

A.A. O'Claire, Kalispel, Mont

A.J. Bigelow, Thermopolis, Wyo

Glen Shipper, Dubois, Wyo

________________________________________________________
(May 29 continued from Jan 8)

1 Sonora L DOR 3 mi No of Adelanto, saved.

10:50 60°

It was now so cold and late we drove fast. First went to Victorville but couldn't get a room. Then to San Bernardino and failed again at the big auro courts. Finally put up at Colton. Put up snakes until 1 AM.

This night was a fine proof that snakes come out when the temperature is ok but go in again when it turns cold; shown by the large number of fresh DORs on a lightly traveled road. I got them alive early in

(Continued on Jan 10th)

Monday, January 10, 1938

8 cards returned today.

Shaw and D?? worked this afternoon.

Bad cold today.

____________________________________________________________
(May 29 continued from Jan 9)

the evening when it was warmer but failed to get any alive ones later. But the few other cars had run over many while they were still out.

Reached Colton plenty tired at 12:20. Miles today 238. Miles of evening desert drive 78.

A very satisfactory day from the standpoint of snakes collected, and new territory surveyed.

Tuesday, January 11, 1938

Stayed home today because of a bad cold.

1 card returned.

Got in some progress on head statistics today and made good headway. While much statistical calculations are still necessary. I feel that this part of the paper is over the peak at last.

Wednesday, January 12, 1938

Jim Devel worked today.

Home today with a cold except one hour.

Shipping the following to Pemberton

1 case containing 12 1/2 gal MT jars.

1 Paper box containing 4-1 gal MT jars

1 Gal bottle formalin

2 pisols

Tags

Scissors (new)

Directions

On the south Palomar grade at 4200 ft. Charles F. Schnack dug up a L. Zonata out of a rock pile at the depth of about 5 ft.

^ Thursday, January 13, 1938

3 cards and 3 questionnaires received today.

Worked today and feeling better. Got in some good licks on heard length tonight, tabulating.

Started Omar on tabulating.

_____________________________________________________
(June 3rd continued)

1 Red racer L DOR Meloland Fields

(Lights on at 7:05 Holtville)

1 Gopher M DOR Date City. Fields. Saved head.

1 Small T. marciana COR Date City 7:20.

almost dark. Fields 88°

Edge of the desert at 7:30. Almost dark. 88° 1/3 moon. No wind.

1 Sonora COR Midway Well 8 PM 88°

1 Sonora COR Pilot Know 8:20 PM 86°

Backed over this one.

Reached Yuma at 8:45. Hot.

Started for San Luis at 9 PM. PST from Peach Auto Court.
Reached there at 9:50, 80°.

Not a thing seen. Very disappointing.

Woodhousii heard at one or two points.

1 Gopher COR. Somerton 10:15, 60°. Backed over head.

The temperature this evening was quite variable. Some places were hotter than others. Back in the auto court at 10:15. 82°.

(continued on Jan. 14)

Friday, January 14, 1938

Saw Perkins this noon,

Only 1 card returned today.

Went to a lecture by Claus Mann tonight.

Jim Dewel worked counting rattle scales today.

__________________________________________________________
June 3rd cont from Jan. 13

A very disappointing evening.

Miles in S.D. C. 80. Miles evening drive Imperial Co. 39, Yuma Co. 49, total 88. Total miles of trip so far, 224.

Page Edit History:
  • janetmary 01/14/2013 01:29 PM

^ Saturday, January 15, 1938

Spent the entire day on head length and made good progress. Plotted the rest of the H-L relationship. Then drew the ones of best fit by eye. Then drew sample groups of curves for example and comparative purposes.

1 card returned today.

_____________________________________________________________
(June 4th cont)

going up the road toward Oracle Jnct which we reached at 9:15. Returned to Tuscon at 10:20, not having seen a thing on the road, dead or alive. There was 1/3 moon. A little breeze. The temp varied from 74 to 88° depending on altitude and exposure. We saw lovejoys snake show at Oracle Junction, but he had nothing particularly interesting. He gets scutes around Oracle Junction but Cinerous ??? are more common. Most of his snakes came from around Owl's Head.

Miles today, daylight 242, night drive 51; total 293.

Perkins told me today that one small trio of his trip had accidentally bitten another in striking for good. The bite was in the jaw. There was considerable swelling but it son went down. No ill effect.

Page Edit History:
  • janetmary 01/14/2013 01:39 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Sunday, January 16

Not very good headway today - too many lunches and dinner worked on head-length ratio of dwarfed races.

_________________________________________________________
(June 5 continued)

found at Casa Grande; the nearest to Tuscon are from Cortaro. She had 40 tigers last year. Of the 70000 cinereous which she has handled the largest was 6'4" N 6'5". Only 4 or 5 were larger than 6'.

We then called on Betty Wooden III and his parents the Haskells at Rincon Ranch about 25 mi. E. of Tuscon at the foor of the Rincon Mts. and talked snakes most of the afternoon. The youngster is intensely interested in the subject. From Rincon ranch he had gophers, piceiis, spotted nights, king snakes (splendida) and Rhino cheilus. the ranch is a very pleasant place with all the necessaries including a swimming pool.

We returned via Bail and the Benson highway.

Cnenumdophorus noted at Vail.

1 Arizona M DOR Rita, Pima Co. Brush desert.

We returned to Tuscon at 5 PM and rested up for the evening drive.

(Continued on Jan. 17)

Monday, January 17, 1938

Page Edit History:

Tuesday, Janurary 18, 1938

No cards today.

worked a short time on dwarf races tonight.

____________________________________________________________
(June 5th cont. from Jan. 17)

1 H.T. DOR Ajo Junction.

1 Cinerisois M COR 3 mi. N. of San Xainei Mission. On the berm. 9:55, 82°. mesquite.

1 P.d. decuitetus S. COR 4 mi. N. of San Xavier Mission. this was right at the reservation boundary. 10:18, 84°.

1 H.T. DOR 1 mi. S. of Ajo Junction.

Reached the auto camp at 10:50 and drove 8 mi. down the Nogales road.

Finally turned in at 11:30. Temp 78-82°.

A great night for Phyllorhynchus. The last luck of the trip so far.

Miles today - daylight 92; evening drive 102; total 194.

The 5 and 10 reading glasses are working fine.

One P. browhi evacuated a gecko? egg capsule.

Page Edit History:
  • janetmary 01/14/2013 02:34 PM

Wednesday, January 19, 1938

Went to Los Angeles on the morning train and returned in the evening.

One questionnaire returned today.

___________________________________________________________
(June 7 continued)

1 H.T. (solare) DOR Curtises Cochise Co.

2 do ??????????????????

1 Petuophia L DOR 9 mi SE of St. David. Rolling mesquite prairie.

Calley 4 mi. NW of Tombstone.

Hunted for a short time under rubbish at Fairbank but got nothings.

Took the side road to the Ft. Huachuca and ate lunch there. 25th Infantry (colored) stationed there. Very interesting place. Found the road to Camille wasn't open so went back to highway P2.

Hunted in Yuccas on a high wind-swept prairie in Cochise Co just east of the Santa Cruz Co line. This may be called Mescal Cruz Co line. This may be called Mescal Spring, Cochise C. Saw a holbrookia and a ?nemi (perplexus?) and collected a collared lizard. There are many fallen yuccas here and they are the only places of concealment but the reptiles under them are few. Probably too cold. We got negative results near Rincon Ranch, under yuccas a few days.

(Cont on Jan. 20

Notes:

janetmary

Check species names. Not sure on one of them.

Page Edit History:
  • janetmary 01/14/2013 02:42 PM

Thursday, January 20, 1938

2 cards back today.

To historical society dinner tonight to hear Marston talk on old times.

______________________________________________________
(June 7 continued from Jan. 19)

before.

Hunted in the river at Patagonia and got a couple of Rana pysiens and a C.S. perplexus.

1 P. solare DOT at Nogales.

Started north for the Pena Blanca spring at 4 PM. The service station man said there was little water int he spring - a forest service ranger said there was plenty. The former was right. The road to the spring is good but unpaved. At the spring the overflow was diverted to a swimming pool in which there were a couple of Ran pipiens. There were no pools any size. We went on 9 miles over an improved but very twisty mountain road to BEar Canyon in the Tamacacore Mts. Here there were a few pools and we collected some tadpoles. Could find no frogs or toads under rocks. Collected a S. Clarkii at Pena Blanca on the return trip and saw several others.

Ate supper (out of a can) at the junction 6 mi. N. of Nogales and started north on the evening drive at 7:45.

(continued on Jan 21)

^ Friday, January 21, 1938

Jim and Chas worked this afternoon.
Only 1 card returned today.
DOg got run over tonight. One
leg seems badly hurt.
Company tonight - little done.
______________________________________________________________
(June 7 Cont from Jan 20)
It was a fine night, little breeze, warm,
2/3 moon. The first part of the trip was
Upper Sonoran. Not a thing was seen
alive or dead. Evidently nothing out as
as there was enough traffic to produce DORs.
1 P. Solare DOR Carmen 82 degrees
Armado at 8:45 78 degrees
Reached Tuscan at 10 PM 80 degrees
Took the trip to the museum in the hop
of finding a Phyllerhynchus. Still no luck
Returned to Tuscan at 10:50. Got the
same cottage again.
It was 80 degrees at San Xavier Mission at 10:30.
Had hoped to get a tree - snake on the
road toward Ruby.
A tough luck day for specimens
of there ever was one.
Miles today daylight 204; Evening 73;
total 277. Total for the trip to date 1180

Saturday, January 22, 1938

Worked all day on the head length
paper. Completely revised the dwarf write up.
OK this time i think.
______________________________________________________________
(June 8th Cont)
Gloyd and others have stripped all the
good rock flakes and we were too tired
to go to more distant places.
The country to the wrath of Marnell
does not look good for night collecting
although there are some fur rock outcrops.
Peoples valley is like a high prairie.
Collard Ingrid noted in Peoples Valley. Also
1 P.d. hernandesi DOR and 1 gopher S
DOR. fields.
S. magister DOR. 5 mi. S. g Kirkland Junction
1 gopher L COR 4 mi. S. g Kirkland Junction
5:30 P.M. grass and scattered rocks. Quite
a fighter. Struck uncounsciously and rattled.
also collard ? DOR here.
Hunted in fair rocks just alone grand
View (3 mi S. of Glen Oaks) hoping to get a
Xentura but no luck. GOt U.O. symmetrical,
C.Q. prplexus, S. magister, and H. texana.
Reached Prescott at 7:15; clear and cool,
After supper drove up and down the road
a few miles hoping to hear frogs, But
didn't so turned in. Miles today 251.
To bed at 10; earliest this week.

Sunday, January 23, 1938

Continued work on head length. Made
good progress. Now up to the final
discussion of species differences. Went
to La Jolla tonight.
______________________________________________________________
(June 9th Continued)
points and collected one or two. One
continued a large fresh skelly. Several
were well plastered with tar below. This was
dry. There was no fresh tar in the road. It
was difficult to see how they had ?

S.D. Co.
Arrived home at 5 P.M., Clear and
cool. Miles today 235; M S.D. Co. 96;
total for the trip 1154
If the trip proved anything it was
that July is too late in the season
except for toads which were thinck and
acture in Southern Arizona, Maybe the
snakes are not immidiately after a rain
Would like to try it. But the spring is
probably best, although the weather would
be a gamble. A cold spell might be
struck and this would mean total
failure.

with trees in the deeply eroded bottoms.
If magister occurs here it ought to

territories where the road is paved.
4 mi.E. of Panoche we hunted in

garter snake. The frogs were quite plentiful.
The garter was in the open behind a suck,
This was at 3:30 PM and warm. The frogs
stuck to the bottom but as the creek was
shallow, were easily caught. The creek was
odonous. Sulpher? This was in San Benito Co
hooked at a roadwide pool at Jameson,
Fresno Co. Pour a Rama a. draytonii and
caught a Boyles King crawling in the open.
This was at 4:50 PM. Warm.

Reptile Club tonight

Both kinds of yuccas are found here.

Quail Spring, and ate lunch at the spring
at 12:30. It was hot got a uta alive here
and saw a magister but did not get him.
The road was pretty tough. We got stuck once
but only for a few moments.

Got a skelly also.

several kinds of lizards. Also a mitch
under a rock.

Turned him loose.
Cally DOR 1 mi E. of 29 Palms

National Monument was interesting. There
are many good rocky areas and five
stands of yuccas but the road is rather
poor.

Sunday, April 10, 1938

I today studied the differences between Eumeces skiltonianus and E.g. rubricaudatus. Taylor gives the following differences:

Rubri Skilt

Supralabials Usually 8 Usually 7

Interparietal Not usually enclosed Enclosed

Using a bunch of large unicolored specimens, and 3 with real pink tails while quite small, we find all unenclosed and all but, on one side with 8 supras.

D??? some clearly skilts and some questionable we find that enclosure is a poor key, for about 1/2 are unenclosed. Some of the larger ones which are bright. But tho supras are all seven except in one spec. which is 7-8 and another which is 8-8. So this is a better character than the parietal. Best of all seems to me the shape of the ??? parietal. For in skilt this is sharply wedge shaped, while rubri is it more blunt and tends more toward parallel sided, although it is not really parallel sided.

Got started today on the diary notes. Finished the first drafts.

continued on April 9th)

Thursday, April 14, 1938

Ate some Crotalus reber today, prepared by ??? Perkins. Some fried and rolled bread crumbs and some saute. Tasted good more like rabbit than chicken. A little tough because it was very fresh.

Pemberton returned today and brought all my material back and the specimens he took. He came around to the house tonight and stayed an hour and a half telling me all about his trip. Lost one of my pistols on Marie Magdalena.

The material is contained in 8-2 qt. jars and 1 live racer from Clarion. He said luck was only fair. He said Burt also collected snakes and got 2 not contained in my material a coral like snake (zapecs.) from Isabel Island and a snake with a ring on the neck (tantilla?) from Maria Magdalena.

Pemberton has no plans for trips in the immediate future.

Perkins reports 2 DOR spec

1 Ru????, 1 gopher both Mission Gorge

Notes:

janetmary

Check species names.

Sunday, April 17, 1938

Completed more notes.

This afternoon Bob Hoard called with the specimens he had collected in southeastern Sonora. There were two snakes and good series of lizards. He reports the road quite good as far as Guaymas.

The season was too early for good collecting. Quite cold at night. He reports that the snakes in that area come out after the rains in July in the Hermosillo area probably May would be the best season.

He did not shoot specimens but caught them alive with the help of Mexican kids.

He had only 1 DOR record not represented by a specimen: 1 sidewinder 12 mi. E. of Holtville.

Page Edit History:
  • janetmary 04/05/2013 11:46 AM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

^ Monday, April 18, 1938

Heard Prof. Allen of Cornell talk on Hudson Bay birds tonight at the meeting of the Fellows.

Sherwin told me today that his wife found in their garden at Point Loma about 2 weeks gao 2 balls of ringneck snakes each about as big as her fist and guessed to contain 20 snakes. There were just below ground surface and were dug up. There were not dormat and crawled quickly away.

_____________________________________________________________

At the Rotary Club at Escondido I was told that shrikes impale both lizards and small snakes on barbed wire fences and thorns. They don't seem to return to eat them. Mostly garter snakes.

Reported by Gander

1 gopher S. Flinn Spr. Not collected 3 P.M.

Saturday, April 23, 1938

Spent the day identifying Bob Hoard's Sonora material, preparing the head length paper for the press and other miscellaneous work. Made fair progress.

B.C. Cain of Oakland called in the afternoon. He is on this way to the desert. Loaned him a Winchester single shot.

Chas Shaw worked all day and made good headway counting scales. Every rattler is counted up to date and the harmless snakes that are usually counted nearly so.

Bogert phoned from LA tonight.

Wednesday, May 4, 1938

Started for San Francisco this afternoon at 1:05. Clear and warm but after several days of cold weather. With GG and Mrs. Pff.
53 miles to the County Line - nothing seen.
Went via Sunland and Tujunga.

1 Red Racer L |DOR| Pacoima, LA Co. Black head. Orchard.
1 Gopher L |DOR| Castaic Grass.

Turned west just beyond Wheeler Ridge PO on State Highway 166 via Taft, McKittrick, Blackwell's Corner and thence to Paso Robles on US466, where we spent the night. That part of the road on the west side of the San Joaquin Valley looked fine but not a thing was seen. It was evidently too cool and too soon after cold weather. We were traveling fast and might have missed a small snake but certainly would not have missed a large one. Had much trouble with the car overheating and was seriously worried. Didn't discover until next day that the radiator shutter was closed tight. Arrived at Paso Robles at 9:15. Miles today 337

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 07/22/2013 04:59 PM

Thursday, May 5, 1938

Started from Paso Robles this morning at 8:20. Cool and windy. Not a thing seen all the way to Palo Alto. Arrived at 12:40. Had much engine trouble and had to fill the car with water frequently. Had it fixed in Palo Alto while lunching. Mrs. Pfeft went on to San Francisco by train.

Talked to Philip in the early afternoon, then saw Nute of the Stanford Press about the head dimensions paper. He can't get it ont for two weeks at least.

In the evening was initatied into Tou Beta Pi and gave them a talk on Innovators and Inventions after the dinner.

Miles today 199

Szlyna

Friday, May 6, 1938

Left Pally for San Francisco this morning at 8:40. Clear and cool. Arrived at 9:48. Conferred with Fox.
Met GG at the Palace at 12 and left immediately for Berkley. Spend 1 1/4 hrs at MVZ. Saw Grinnell, Ritter, T.S. Palmer, and Rodgers. Had quite a chat with Palmer about the Death Valley expedition of 1891.
Rodgers is working on Cnemidophorus and Eumeces. He is using statistics and is interested in some of my forms.

Left at 3. Went via the new Broadway Tunnel, Walnut Creek, Dublin, and Tracy, Manteca, and south on 99. Had supper at Fresno at 8. It was fairly warm but not a thing was seen. Might have passed up a couple because of the high speed.

Arrived at Bakersfield at 10:50; quite cool now. Put up at the Motel. Miles today 348.

Saturday, May 1, 1938

This morning started for Walker's Pass at 8:30. It was clear and quite warm.

1 Crotaphytus silus |DOR| Loma Park.

Hunted for a short time in Granite at the canyon entrance 12 miles E. of Bakersfield.

1 M. lateralis L |DOR| Hobo Hot Springs. Skellies were seen here. Not collected.

Hunted near Isabella. Got skellies and utas. Saw utas and whips.
Stopped 4 mi. E. of Onyx. Here there are plenty of tree yuccas. The first were only a couple of miles west. Got 2 Xantusia virgilis. Saw one under the first dead yucca and lost him. Was encouraged to keep trying but it was hard to get any as they seem scarce. Saw utas and skellies.

Hunted in rocks 10 mi. E. of Onyx.
This is called Camebroke and is in Weldon Valley. Got skellies here.
Hunted in Yuccas just east (a few hundred yards) of Walker's Pass (5248 ft)
X.V. were more plentiful than near Onyx. Also saw utas.

1 Leopard Lizard |DOR| Freeman Junction.
From Freeman Junction we drove north on US395 to Olancha
(Continued on May 2)

Saturday, May 14, 1938

Started out from Indio this morning at 8:30. It was clear and hot.
We first visited Walker's Snake Pit at Indian Wells. He said the largest Cinereous he had ever caught out of 7000 in 7 years was 5'7". He had a mitch from 5 mi. up the Palms to Pines Highway from the junction. Sidewinders are best hunted at sun-up. They are trailed to the end of their tracks. If you go out too late they have already gone down mammal holes for the day. Snakes seem less plentiful now in the sand hills about Indian Wells than they were a few years ago.

1 Cally shot at Cathedral City
1 Sonora |DOR| Cathedral City sandy desert
1 Arizona L |DOR| Palm Springs Brushy desert. saved
1 Gopher M |DOR| Palm Springs Brushy desert
1 Arizona M |DOR| Palm Springs Brushy desert
1 Arizona L |DOR| Palm Springs Station sandy desert

Reached the Morongo Road Junction, now called Alameda at 10:05. Now quite hot.
A whiptail shot 5 mi. N. of Alamesa.
1 Red Rattler |DOR| 1 mi. S. of Morongo Lodge. Brush.
Saved head. This probably first specimens from San Bernardino Co.
1 Red Racer M |DOR| Morongo Valley Brush.
Hunted at the upper end of the Morongo Valley and got utas, whip, and xantusia vigilis.

(Continued on March 21)

Monday, May 16, 1938

Hoard reports a California King from S.D.

Heard at the reptile club tonight Chucks can't be deflated by puncturing. Coyotes eat rattlers.
Orcutti was seen in a tree quite a distance from granite at Glen Lonely.
The natures in certain parts of South America think that geckos bite sea-lions and kill them quickly.
Saw specimens of Bufo Californicus from Mission Gorge.

Checked up with Mrs Leslie and Omar today. Omar needs work. Got my guns and collecting materials from Tony Green. Recd a Phylorhynchus brown, a female from Vic Householder today.

(May 20th Continued)

1 Leafnose L |COR| Coline (=Bensons) 70°, 9:04, Windy

Wednesday, May 18, 1938

Out to dinner tonight.

(May 21 Continued)

Of Palm Springs - Indio and Palms to Pines highways. Had a fine afternoon talking over Cowles experiments and other matters.

Started out again at 4:25. Cool and windy. Drove down to Mecca and then to Shaver Summit where we ate supper.

1 Gopher L |DOR| 2 mi. S. of Indio. Low brush desert
1 Mccallii |DOR| 3 mi. E. of Mecca
1 Patchnose L |DOR| Shaver Summit. Greasewood Desert.

Started west at 6:40. Quiet. Just sundown. Went at high speed to junction with aqueduct road a couple of miles out from 99 on 60-70. Then started the real evening drive at 7:11. It was dusk, not quite dark. Some breeze - 80°. As the evening wore on it cooled rapidly and a strong wind came up. No more moon tonight.

1 Sonora L |COR| at 1 mi. N. of this junction. Call this 3 mi. E. of Indio. 7:16 80°
1 Gecko |COR| 7:22 same.

Went up the first camp branch and not a good mitch. 7:33, 78°. Bush and rocks. Very little wind up the canyon. Not quite dark. Fargo Canyon.

1 Sonora |COR| at Berdoo Canyon Branch.

Reached home at 10:15. Clear and warm. Miles in S.D. Co. 70. Total today 166. Total for the trip 554. The lack of specimens along the road and especially over the Palms to Pines highway shows how the cold weather of the last few days has curtailed reptile activity. Last nights poor results were typical.

Spent the afternoon and evening catching up. Shaw worked today and yesterday. Robt Hoard reports a DOR red racer at Rosarita Beach, B.C.

Saturday, May 28, 1938

This morning we started from Reno at 9:30. It was part cloudy and cold. It had rained last night. The temperature at 10 AM was 55 degrees. Tough luck.
Skelly seen at Washoe, Washoe Co.
Hunted in the rocks at Lakeview, Washoe Co. at 9:30, 60F, and got several skellies sunning themselves on the rocks. Still cold and windy. No DORs where many were seen last summer.
1 Gopher S. DOR Carson City, grass
1 T.s. infernalis L DOR Minden, Douglas Co., hw. Plenty red. Gardens.
1 Taeniatus Shot in the brush by Shorty where we hunted for a while at Topaz Lake, 2 mi. S. of the State Line. This was a brushy-rocky area and the lizard hunting was good. Whips were especially plentiful; we also got utas, skellies and a leopard lizard.
Skelly seen at Rancho Jan Karlos, Mono Co.
From here on until we reached Sherwin Grade, north of Bishop it was too high and cold for reptiles.
This was about 100 miles.
(continued on Jan.1)

Wednesday, June 1, 1938

Saturday, June 4, 1938

This morning we left Yuma eastbound at 9:50 MST. All times hereafter in Arizona are MST.

Dips were noted at Dublin; also callys and whiptails. Chucks were seen in the Gila Mountains as usual. Umas were seen at Welton and dips at Asher.

We stopped to talk with Hale for a while but he had nothing of interest. Said reptiles were very scarce the last 2 years, but he always says that.

Dips were noted at Kim and Le Sage, Yuma Co. It was very hot from here on and the lack of DORs was notable.
Reached Bela Loma at 1:45; the man at the service station had nothing of interest.

A dip was noted 14 mi. W. of Casa Grande. It was 11:20 here today; 110 in the car at Picacho.

Cnemidophorus noted at Marana.
P. Solare at Jaynes Station.

Arrived at Tucson at 4:40; 96°. Several specimens dead from the heat including the boa we had brought for Woodin.
We started the evening drive at 7:50
(Continued on Jan 15)

Monday, June 6, 1938

This morning we were up at 5:30 and on the road at 6:15 looking for dead snakes, and also to have a lizard hunt. It was clear and warm - not overcast and sultry as on previous mornings lately.

We just went across to San Xavier Mission. Found a P.d. descurtatus DOR in fairly good shape 2 mi. N. of the Mission. Saved it. Well pleased with this. We then drove north on the road skirting the Tucson Mts. but found no DORs. Then went west on the Ajo road 3 mi. W. of the junction and hunted in mixed cactus, brush, and mesquite. Got a number of callys and whips. One of the latter had the wings of a cicada protruding from his mouth. Found a coleonyx under a dried steer carcass. Lost a horned toad near the junction of Congress and Grand. Went north on the Oracle road about 21 miles but got no DORs. Noted callys at 12 and 15 miles out of Tucson. Returned to the cabin at 10:20. Somewhat cooler than yesterday. Pickled specimens and wrote up dairy. Miles morning drive 74

(Continued on Feb. 27th)

Tuesday, June 7, 1938

Today we took a trip from Tcson via Benson, Fairbank, and Patagonia to Nogales. Then a side trip to Bear Canyon on the raod to Ruby in the Tumacacori Mts, thence back to Tucson. It was an interesting trip but very poor from a collecting standpoint. Too late for the spring specimens - too early for those which come out with the summer rains. The total absence of specimens in a long night drive through what should be good territory was particularly disappointing.

We left Tucson at 8:55; clear and warm. Callys were noted at Tucson and Wilmot. Also a P. Solare at Wilmot, Pima Co. Cally noted at Rankin, Pima Co.; H.T. at Rita, Pima Co.

1 H.T. |DOR| Pantano, Pima Co.
1 Cinereous S. |DOR| Pantano mesquite
1 Cornutum |COR| 9 mi. W. of Benson just East of the Pima-Cochise Co. line.
1 Cinereous S |DOR| Benson, Cochise Co. Brushy desert.

Reached Benson at 10:15 - warm.

1 Leopard lizard |DOR| Benson.
Shot a cally and whip here.
1 H.T. (Solare) 3 mi. S. of Benson |DOR|.
Observed whiptails at St. David.

Wednesday, June 8, 1938

This morning we started from Tucson for Phoenix at 9:45. It was clear and warm. Quite hot at Phoenix; got cooler beyond Wickenburg and was very comfortable at Prescott. Called for mail at Tuscon and got everything except the papers.

1 P. Solare L |DOR| Jaynes Station, saved.

Had the usual trouble with the car boiling away water rapidly, or throwing it out, all the way but particularly between Tucson and Phoenix.

Saw Evans at Phoenix. He did not have much that was interesting. He had a black racer from Florence Junct. I learned from him that the little P. Browni secured from Housholder came from Enchanto Valley in the Enchanto Mts, near River Road, 7 mi. W. of Cave Creek.

1 Gopher L |DOR| Glendale fields.

The road south of Wickenburg is being rebuilt and will not be so good. Too fast - too many banks and cuts.

Cally |DOR|. Wickenburg, 9 mi. NW of Wickenburg and Congress Junct.

Collard lizard |DOR| 4 mi. SW of Yarnell. Hunted at the type of locality of X. Arizonae 1 mi. S. of Yarnell and got a H. Texana.

(Cont. on Jan. 22)

Thursday, June 9, 1938

This morning we started from Prescott at 7:10 MST. It was clear and cool. We hunted in granite 2 mi. N. of Prescott where there were a few cap-rocks and got a uta stans. The granite is not well flaked.

We hunted at Willow Creek which is just north of Jerome Junction. There is a fine creek here with many granite boulders which however, do not flake well. Hoped to get a Xantusia but found nothing under any granite flakes or cap rock. Probably too cold in the winter. Other lizards were plentiful and we secured a number.

1 P.d. Hernandesi |DOR| Chino Valley, Yavapai Co.
1 Skelly shot on the road at Del Rio, Yava. Co.
1 Cnemidophorus shot and a collard lizard caught at Del Rio.
Collard lizard shot at Drake, Yavapai Co.
Collard lizard seen at Rok, Yavapai, Co.

Collard lizards and skellies seen and shot at Rok, Yavapai Co. and at Prairie, Yavapai Co.

Collard lizards were very plentiful along the road from Paulden north on rocks. They were large and a number were beautifully green in color. We stopped at several

(Continued on Jan. 23rd)

Friday, June 10, 1938

This morning we started west from Holbrook at 7:20. It was clear and warm. I still hoped to get a nuntuis in the morning as I had done on the way to the Snake Dance. We reached Waislow at 8:07; clear and warm. NOt a DOR in this 33 miles which should have been fuitful. We now went north across the prairie on the unpaved road to Leupp Trading Post. Here we inquired about roads and caught a B. woodhousii. We returned to the highway on the road via Canyon Diablo RR station. Stopped to hunt in sandstone (a fine outcrop) 6 mi. SW of Leupp but got only 1 uta. This was at 9:30 but lizards did not seem to be out. Maybe too cool and breezy. A collard lizard was caught 10 mi. SW on Leupp. A collard lizard was seen at the Canyon Diablo RR Station.

We hunted on the edge of Canyon Diablo between the highway at Two guns and the RR Sta. got several lizards. We next went down the Meteor Crater side road, which is in very bad condition, for 3 mi. and hunted in red sandstone. Got several lizards. We then returned to the highway and started west. 1 C.s. Perplexus |DOR| 3 mi. W. of Winona

Saturday, June 11, 1938

This morning we started from Las Vegas at 9:30. It was slightly overcast, warm and sultry. We first went up the Indian SPrings road towards Beatty. Only went up this road 10 miles and then turned back. Shot a couple of whiptails 9 miles from Las Vegas.

A couple of P. Platyrhinos were caught on the road 6 mi. NW of Las Vegas. A cally was DOR 10 mi. NW of Las Vegas. A cally was DOR 10 mi. NW of Las Vegas. We hunted along a couple of ditches for R. onca but had no luck. What appeared to be a bull frog was seen in the lake at Lorenzi Lake Park.

We again left Las Vegas on US 91 at 11:05. It was cool, part cloudy, and quite windy.

1 Arizona L |DOR| Bracken, Clark Co., Sandy Desert light brush.
1 Platyrhinos |DOR| Jean
1 Large female tortoise alive on the road at Jean.
1 Gopher S. |DOR| Borax, Clark Co. Light brush, desert 84°
1 Platyrhinos |DOR| Mountain Pass S.B. Co.

At Clark Mountain Station got 4 Xantusia vigilis. Saw whiptails and utas.

Sunday, June 12, 1938

This morning we started home from San Bernardino at 8 o'clock, stopping for breakfast at Riverside. It was cold and cloudy.

1 Red Racer L |DOR| bet. Perris and Elsinor grass
1 Patchnose M |DOR| NOrth Elsinore Brush-grass.
1 Gopher L |COR| Fallbrook Brush Orchard. Turned him loose.
1 Boyles King L |DOR| Buena Orchards.
1 Gopher S |DOR| San Marcos grass.

Arrived home at 11:45. Part cloudy and cold.
Miles in San Diego County 69.
Miles today 132
Total miles for the trip 2604

The trip was good sport. The collecting was poor partly because of unseasonable weather - partly through lack of knowledge of the proper season in which to collect in some areas. The highlights were the Phyllorhynchus at Tucson and the pyrrhus on the Arizona side at Boulder Dam.

Spent the afternoon and evening catching up. Jim Deuel worked today and helped materially in taking care of the incoming material.

Monday, June 13, 1938

Chas. Shaw worked today and made headway with the many incoming specimens.

Had a long talk with Bob Hoard yesterday about his trip. Agreed to pay $50 towards his expenses and furnish him with various collecting materials. He is to have the privilege of writing up his material first in connection with his masters thesis. I can then use the material in any write-ups as I see fit. Novel items were left somewhat undecided; I am to describe them if they belong to groups in which I have worked.

Bob called tonight for the jars; the other collecting material will be gathered later.

Gander reports a red racer DOR Lake Hodges June 8.

Thursday, June 23, 1938

The Campbells of 29 Palms called this morning. Also a party named Martin from Florida in the afternoon.

Hill of Los Angeles came at 11 and left a number of specimens that Mosauer collected at Acapulco to be identified.

American Society of Ichthyologists and Herpetologists, Western Division
(Report by Margaret Storey)

More than twenty members and guests met informally at the laboratory and home of Laurence M. Klauber on Friday afternoon and visited his unsurpassed collection of southwestern rattlesnakes and other herpetological specimens. On Saturday a night desert collecting trip arranged by C.B. Perkins, of the San Diego Zoo, yielded eleven live snakes of seven species in four hours in the vicinity of The Narrows. In addition, fourteen snakes of ten species and two lizards were observed run over on the road. Some of these were in sufficiently good condition to be saved. The National American Society of Ichthyologists and Herpetologists meeting at Berkeley from July 20 to 23 prevented official participation in the American Association for the Advancement of Science meetings this year. Science Sept. 2, 1928

Saturday, July 2, 1938

This morning we started eastward from Casa Grande at 7:40; it was clear and cool.

Dead Bufo Alvarius were noted at Arizola, Toltec, Eloy all Pinal Co.

We hunted for awhile in brush and suhuaras at Wynola, Pinal Co, and got a considerable number of lizards. Cally was the only one seen and not taken. We also found a live desert tortoise in the Suhuara forest here. We left this point at 10:40.

At Red Rock, Pinal Co Bufo Alvaruis was evident in a muddy irrigation pool by the roadside. There were a number of clasping pairs which would drive to the bottom together when one in sight. We collected here in mesquite and got assorted lizards including scaly lizards. Callies were seen but not collected.

At Naviska, Pina County whiptails and Alvaruis DOR and a solare was caught on the road. Alvaruis also DOR at Marana, Rillito, Sabino, Cortaro, Kino and Jaynes all in Pima Co.
Everywhere toads were much in evidence compared with a month ago - one difference

(Continued on Feb. 10)

Sunday, July 3, 1938

This morning we got up rather late because we were out so late last night. It was 8:30 before all specimens were taken care of and the car packed; and 9:15 before we got started from Tucson. It was clear and warm, not hot.

1 Gila Monster L |DOR| 11 mi. N. of Tucson. Mesquite and Cactus

Cally seen 2 mi. S. of Oracle Junct.
Hunted in brush and cactus 4 mi. N. of Oracle Junction at 10:30. Cool and breezy and very comfortable. Got a few lizards.

Hunted in rocks 4 mi. S. of Owl Head. Pinal Co. Collared Lizard, U.O. Symmetrica and callies were seen. A small DOR gila monster was picked up here and saved. Scattered cactus mesquite and brush. It was too breezy and late in the morning for good hunting. A large cally seen at Florence also B. Alvarius.

Monday, July 4, 1938

This morning we started from Blythe at 8:30. It was clear and warm-somewhat warmer than on previous days.
Whiptail seen 3 mi. W. of Blythe. Hunted here a few moments in mesquite. N.G.

Cally and Dip seen 6 mi. W. of Blythe = Mesa Station.
Whiptails seen 7 and 12 mi. W. of Blythe.

We hunted for a while 15 mi. W. of Blythe, between 9:30 and 10. Got a number of Uta Graciosa and various other lizards. The utas were hanging head downward on greasewood. The bodies were a perfect color match with the gray limbs of the bushes. They could be spotted by looking carefully along each vertical branch. Sometimes they could scared to the base of the branches and then shot.

Chas. Shaw found a red racer eating a small patchnose. He had only about 2 inches of the pachnose down but it seemed quite dead. The patchnose contained a mouse and some round worms in the stomach. One of the callies caught here contained a dragon fly (large).

Whiptail seen at 17 mi. W. of Blythe. We hunted for a while 21 mi. W. of

(Continued on Feb. 17)

Monday, July 11, 1938

M. Graham Netting arrived this noon. Saw him tonight at the Reptile Club where he gave a good talk with colored slides.

He showed a picture of a Penna Horridus with a complete and definitely outlined stripe from head to tail; the boylii - California transformation over again. Not the uneven and indefinite strip of atricaudatus.

Tuesday, July 19, 1938

Spent the entire day at MVZ; first preparing the specimens for exhibition with the assistance of Tom Rodgers - second discussing herpetological problems, particularly the definition of species. Looked at Bensons recent acquisitions from Sonora - a good lot - and Rodgers material from the Providence mountains. Went to lunch with Netting, Grant, and Myers.

Spent the evening from 6 to 8:30 at a meeting of the Board of Governors of the I and H Society.

The specimens look good but are a very meager collection. Broke by glasses this morning, a great inconvenience.

Thursday, July 21, 1938

Went over to San Francisco on business this morning at 8:30 and returned at 3:30 in time to conduct the final business meeting of the ASIAH society. The attended movies in a joint meeting with the mammalogists until 5:45. Saw Vorhies pictures of cinereous eating rabbits. The most interesting points were the use of fangs to aid in drawing the food and rubbing in a rock to push the food down into the stomach when it was partially down. The latter may have been accidental.

In the evening went to the joint dinner with the mammal Society. Said a few words in cooperation.

Tanner says he has many more concolor and will let me borrow them. Saw his worm snake paper. He will trade specimens. Ellis will trade literature. Saw Walter T. Taylor today.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 09/24/2013 01:09 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Friday, July 22, 1938

This morning went down to Stanford to hear the last ASIAH papers. Arrived there at 10 and returned to Berkeley at 5. Good papers. Impressed by Twitty's Triturus results. Spent part of the afternoon in the Natural History Museum where geo Myers is making great improvements. Met a number of more Ichs and Herps.

Ate supper at a noted fish joint with Grants, Storers, Nettings, and others. Talked over I+H matters with Netting.

1 Gopher L |DOR| first town S. of Redwood fields.

Szlyna

Unsure about Twitty's Triturus?

Saturday, July 23, 1938

Spent the morning until 11:30 packing up specimens at MVZ and trading with Rodgers and Fitch. Then went over to CAS and saw the gang just leaving for the zoo. Lunched with Slevin. Then left SF at 3:30. Went via Gilroy and Hollister to the Pinnacles, arriving at 7:30. 1 Garter (sutalis) lost on the road just south of Tres Pinos. Got a few frogs in the evening. Plenty deer about. The frogs came up under the oaks lake toads. There were plenty of tadpoles about.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 09/24/2013 01:15 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Sunday, July 24, 1938

This morning we left the Pinnacles at 10:40. It was clear and warm. We went down the road to the junction near the CCC camp and then went 2 miles NW to the end of the road. Got a skelly on the way. Walked up the canyon for maybe 1/4 mile and got a skelly and a number of frogs. Saw one large whiptail and a M. Lateralis DOR. The frogs were in caves with pools at the bottom.

The country does not look anything like Xantusia vigilis territory. It is a transition territory with pines and other trees all about. There are no Yuccas, at least where I was. While there are plenty of rocks, and more high up where we did not go, they are no smooth and they do not flake. A few chunks were pried off without result. A few more frogs were taken along the creek on the way out and another skelly or two. All were within the monument.

We hunted at a sheep ranch 3 mi. E. of Panoche and got a skelly. Saw no reason to expect magister here and none was seen. It is barren, foothill

Cont. on Feb. 19

Saturday, August 13, 1938

Bob Hoard came in today and we discussed the results of his trip and looked at his specimens which were left here. A good series of lizards; snakes not so good as the reason was too far advanced. Should go down there in spring. Many of the problems still unsolved although he worked hard and used all the newer collecting methods. I am surprised he got no Xantusias in-spite of turning over many yuccas which were plentiful. He will work the material up as a thesis later. Offered him all my L.C. material from previous collections if he wanted it.

Worked the rest of the day on statistics trying to improve the correlation and chi square forms. Decided to let them go as is. A frightful waste of time but I think I have a better understanding of the situation. The texts are terribly vague, involved, and conflicting. Will stay with the older pre-Fisher methods on correlation.

Duel worked this afternoon and evening preserving specimens.

Monday, September 5, 1938

This morning I continued work on the desert night collecting paper and finished the first draft of all but the part citing specific experiences and the tabulation of statistics. Finding that the records as compiled in the field trip books did not lend them selves well to assembling these data I decided to go through all the diaries and relist the desert trips. This is a long hard job but when done will improve the material considerably. Worked the rest of the day and evening on this listing and got as far as August 1933.

Bob Hoard worked on his Lower California material this morning.

Thursday, September 15, 1938

At the Gas Assu Convention in Santa Barbara in the morning.
Started south at 1:30 - warm and sultry. Went via Ventura, Santa Paula, Fillmore and Piru to Castoic Junction then up the new Ridge Route to Gorman thence to Lancaster, north to Mohave, east to Kramer Junction, South via 395 to Adelanto, Cajon Pass and San Bernardino.

The south side of the Antelope valley looks poor in the daytime all the way from Quail Lake to a point 6 mi. W. o f Lancaster. Except for the Joshua forest between Fairmont and Neenach it is all stubble fields, grazing land, and a dead pear orchard. No good brush. Would certainly be a waste of time to work this at night. Looks good between Lancaster and Mohave but too much travel.

1 Scute M |DOR| 7 mi. W. of Fairmont, Dead Orchard and Grass.

Hunted for a short while to kill time in the joshuas 6 mi. W. of Fairmont and got a couple of x vigilis under dead stems. They seemed to be quite plentiful

(Continued on Sept. 12)

Wednesday, September 21, 1938

This afternoon at 3 o'clock started for the desert with Gander to check the vegetation on the Borego road. It was hot and sultry after several days of this character.

1 small red racer |DOR| shady Dell Brush Trees.

Arrived at Julian at 4:45; and at Scissors Crossing at 5:20. From here on we made notes on vegetation.

We ate supper at the county line it being then almost dark. No wind. No moon. 6:14; 90°. Plants here are smaller and more scattered than further back, thus accounting for change in snakes. Air temperature and sand temp. 85°. Pavement somewhat warmer.

Started west driving slowly at 6:42. 85°

1 uta stans |COR| 6 mi. E. of The Narrows 7:15 86°
Rather strong breeze in The Narrows. 7:42; 85°.

CH Dammers 4-11-36 No. Cat number.
G good specimen although somewhat faded.
Narrow even light stripes 2 scales wide; mid dorsal dark stripe 6 rows wide.

Also a Cal. King No. 802 L.A. City.
Mottled. A badly broken mid dorsal line. sometimes lengthwise, sometimes crosswise, sometimes spots. Parallel light lines low down on the sides somewhat like mitida. Brown color not so dark.

Saturday, October 29, 1938

Spent the morning on the San Diego County census and practically finished it.

Arrived at Chicago at 1:30. Went to see Schmidt at about 2. Talked over various matters, especially ASIAH committee appointments. Listed the rattlers in the Field Museum collection and was surprised at the number of them. Some from SE are particularly interesting as well as several from Mexico, the most important of which have already been loaned to Gloyd. Also there were 2 fine Rhinocheilus from Mexico and a number of interesting worm snakes. Asked that these be sent one. Schmidt had my worm snake and Rhinocheilus references laid out. He will copy them for me.

Schmidt and I returned to the hotel about 5 where we met Gloyd and had dinner together. Then we discussed miscellaneous matters until after 11. Especially talked species , nomenclature, who was doing what, etc.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:08 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Sunday, October 30, 1938

This morning I completed the SD Co. census table. Studied Taylor's worm snake paper. Did a little work on the night collecting paper.

Gloyd called for me at 10 and we went to the Chicago Academy of Sciences. Here we worked until 6:30 P.M. with time out for lunch with Gloyds and Necker.

Looked over the CAS specimens of Rhinocheilus, Phyllorhynchus, and Arizona. Made lists and asked to have other items shipped, particularly Phyllorhynchus from vicinity of Wickenburg and some worm snakes out of Blanchard's collection.

Made lists of all rattlers in the CAS collection with Gloyd's assistance. Looked at the T-S, and Field recent rattler acquisitions from Mexico. They are interesting. Gloyd gave me scale counts of most of them. ALso of many horridus. Looked over Kauffeldt's uni-colors; Gloyd gave me the counts of the pups.

Went to Gloyd's apartment had a late supper and talked herpetoology until 10:30. Then back to the hotel.

Accounts tonight.

Artran called today to discuss his proposed new book. He stayed in the library about an hour and took 6 books with him.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:53 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Thursday, December 8, 1938

Today went to N.C. and Chula Vista 30 miles nothing seen a very hot day.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:54 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Friday, December 9, 1938

Today drove out to Jamacha, Dehersa, Glen Lonely, Japatul, Terrinotos and home by way of the highway. A hot day following 3 hot days. 78 miles. Nothing seen. Not a lizard.

Talked the collecting paper with Perkins today and got the last of his criticisms.

A little work on lizard field notes tonight.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:55 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Saturday, December 10, 1938

Got in some good licks on the lizard section of the paper today. Finished the Boulder Dam part and got started on the species notes.

Chas Shaw worked today.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:56 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Sunday, December 11, 1938

Read parts 1 and 2 once more and made a few additional corrections.

Worked all day on lizard field notes; made good headway but finally got tired out. Then switched to American worm snake references and got these all lined up in good shape for future work.

Chas Shaw worked today. Checked 3 worm snakes by the new schedule and found it works well. Found a couple in which the supraoculars touch the anterior supralabials.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:57 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Monday, December 12, 1938

Went to La Jolla this evening to the Fellows meeting with Chapman Grant.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:58 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Tuesday, December 13, 1938

Went to Escondido Rotary Club for lunch today. Out by way of Del Mar and Santa Fe Ranch; returned by regular road. Started at 10:45; back at 1:45. A clear warm day 71 miles, nothing seen.

Jim worked today.

Worked on worm snake characteristics this evening.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 05:59 PM

Out to dinner tonight.

Friday, December 16, 1938

Conferred with Perkins at the Zoo on the collecting paper at noon.

Movie tonight.

Started the day with miscellaneous catching up; then hit the lizard field notes and got in some really good licks.

Shaw worked today still classifying the Mexican collections.

Out to dinner tonight.

Election of officers.

Tuesday, December 20, 1938

Shaw worked today.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:03 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Wednesday, December 21, 1938

Philip returned from his European trip today.

Chas worked on Counting Patterns.

Looked over the fang section of the statistical studya with the idea of revising this next. It looks as if it could be worked over in a relatively short time - 2 or 3 months. The temptation is considerable to describe some new subspecies in Arizona, Rhinocheilus, Phyllorhynchus etc, but the rattler series ought to be issued from time to time.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:12 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Thursday, December 22, 1938

Today went out to El Cajon, Paradise Valley, Chula Vista, National City. A cold day after many days of heavy rain. 50 miles. Nothing seen.

Chas Shaw worked today.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:13 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Friday, December 23, 1938

Chas Shaw worked today.

Miscellaneous filing and catching up tonight.
Started Mrs. Leslie on fang tabulation although she hasn't finished the calculation of moments.

Page Edit History:

Saturday, December 24, 1938

Entered all specimens in the record catalogue to date.

Went over to the NH and Zoo and got final criticisms on the collecting paper from Gander and Perkins.

Started work in a small way on the fang paper.

Chas Shaw worked today.

A little done in the morning - otherwise parties, dinners, and visits.

Monday, December 26, 1938

Worked all day on the fang paper and made first-class progress, completing a first and revised draft, down to the statistical part. This must now be completely revised including new data, measurements, and methods.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:16 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Tuesday, December 27, 1938

Had a conference with Mrs. Benchley. Showed her the ms. and got a final OK on taking it to the printer.

Jim Deuel worked today.

Worked on worm snakes tonight preparing a schedule for the boys to work on tomorrow.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:17 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Wednesday, December 28, 1938

The collecting manuscript went to the printers today. How long now before it will be issued?

Deuel and Shaw worked today checking typical worm snakes for the second series of characteristics.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:18 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Thursday, December 29, 1938

Worked for a while tonight on the few tables that have been awaiting the end of the year for completion.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:18 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Friday, December 30, 1938

This noon called at the NH museum and the Zoo. Got some data from Mrs. Leslie.

Cy told me a USC student told him he had found desert tortoises active at night; one with a moon in mid-July at 8 P.M. another time in mid-August no moon. Both times around walks at Piute Butler near Lovejoy Butter, LA Co.

Did a little work on fangs tonight.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:21 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Saturday, December 31, 1938

Spent all day on sexual dimorphism in fang length and correlation of H and F. Made good progress but as usual these long computations go slowly. At least after the L-H battle last winter. I know how to tackle a problem of this type.

Page Edit History:
  • Szlyna 10/29/2013 06:22 PM
  • BPOC 12/07/2010 05:36 PM

Memoranda

Worked all day on the correlation of L and F, and H and F, Platteville series only. Made good progress but these calculations are certainly time consuming.

Lampropeltis getula

California King snake

L.g. boylii refers to the subspecies of king snake which has a ringed pattern.

L.g. californiae refers to the subspecies of king snake which has a striped pattern.
